As a result, the company believes it can still become profitable by the end of 2021 on an adjusted EBITDA basis.</p><p>Uber&#39;s ride-hailing service was hit hard by the pandemic last year as lockdowns diminished the need for trips, a rut that was in large part buttressed by an intense focus on food delivery. Uber&#39; Eats also set a record last month, spiking over 150% year-over-year and hitting a record annual run rate of $52 billion last month.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/uber-eats-doordash-dara-khosrowshahi-2021-4\">Uber is battling DoorDash to rule food delivery. These are the steps Uber&#39;s CEO is taking to topple Eats&#39; biggest rival.</a></em></p><p>The increase in booking in the past month has been largely fueled by optimism surrounding increased vaccination in the US and could be a sign things might be starting to return to normal.</p><p>&#34;As vaccination rates increase in the United States, we are observing that consumer demand for Mobility is recovering faster than driver availability, and consumer demand for Delivery continues to exceed courier availability,&#34; the company said.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/uber-stock\">Uber&#39;s stock rose</a> on the news of a rebound in recovery on Monday, climbing as much as 4% in early trading Monday following the disclosure.</p><p>The need for ride-hailing services is also setting up a potential shortage of drivers for Uber and competitors like Lyft.</p><p>Just last week, Uber<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/uber-spending-250-million-driver-pay-pandemic-shortage-2021-4\"> announced that it plans to spend $250 million on incentives and guarantees for drivers.</a> The move is a part of an effort to get more drivers back on the road following a shortage caused by the COVID-19 pandemic.</p><p>&#34;In 2020, many drivers stopped driving because they couldn&#39;t count on getting enough trips to make it worth their time. In 2021, there are more riders requesting trips than there are drivers available to give them-making it a great time to be a driver,&#34; Dennis Cinelli, the head of Uber&#39;s US and Canada across all 50 states - and none of them did well.</p><p>In a Monday press release, the White House assessed each state&#39;s level of infrastructure and offered &#34;<a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/statements-releases/2021/04/12/white-house-releases-state-by-state-fact-sheets-to-highlight-nationwide-need-for-the-american-jobs-plan/#content\">fact sheets</a>&#34; on where they stand to benefit from President Joe Biden&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pete-buttigieg-biden-infrastructure-bill-transporation-2021-4\">$2 trillion &#34;extreme weather events&#34; as major issues.</p><p>No state managed to get even as high as a C+, much less a B.</p><p>Other states got no grade at all, such as Arkansas, Wyoming, and both src=\"https://i.insider.com/60746a6e2cc1ef0018da138c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Captain Kaitlyn Hernandez, commander, 717th Ordnance Company, 52nd Ordnance Group (Explosive Ordnance Disposal), trains at Hernandez, commander, 717th Ordnance Company, 52nd Ordnance Group (Explosive Ordnance Disposal), trains at Fryar Stadium March 28 in preparation to set the Guinness World Record for the fastest woman to run 1-mile in a bomb suit.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Army</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A female EOD soldier set a new world record for running a mile in a 96-pound bomb suit this month.</li>\n<li>She ran the mile in 10 minutes and 23 seconds, shattering a record set by another soldier in 2013.</li>\n<li>The record for men was set in 2017 by a British Army soldier who ran it in 7 minutes and 24 seconds.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A female US Army soldier set a new Guinness World Record this month for the mile-run in a bomb suit weighing almost 100 pounds, <a href=\"https://www.army.mil/article/245101/defusing_danger_soldier_sets_guinness_world_record\">the service announced recently</a>.</p><p>Wearing the heavy suit, Capt. Kaitlyn Hernandez, commander of the 717th Ordnance Company, 52nd Ordnance Group (Explosive Ordnance Disposal), shattered the previous record of 11 minutes and 6 seconds at the 2nd Annual Bomb Suit Run and Family 5K at George Mason University in Virginia on April 3.</p><p>Running a mile in a little over 10 minutes is not much of a challenge for most members of the armed forces, but running one in a bomb suit is a lot tougher.</p><p>The suits are designed to protect military bomb disposal technicians from a explosive blasts at close range. They are hot, heavy, and can be extremely physically taxing.</p><p>The blast-proof body suit weighs 84 pounds, and the helmet weighs another 12 pounds. </p><p><a href=\"https://www.army.mil/article/245101/defusing_danger_soldier_sets_guinness_world_record\">Talking with the Army about her achievement</a>, Hernandez said that &#34;the helmet&#39;s definitely the worst part because if you&#39;re leaning forward or backward it&#39;ll take your whole body with you.&#34;</p><p>&#34;You never know how the suit is going to affect you,&#34; she said, adding that &#34;sometimes you&#39;re feeling really great, and sometimes it punches you in the face. Windy days are pretty rough too, when you hit a headwind it feels like you&#39;re running in mud.&#34;</p><p>Hernandez said that overcoming the challenges of the suit are largely mental. &#34;It&#39;s usually a split-second, any time I run and start feeling sorry for myself I just have to get over it and say it&#39;s not that bad,&#34; she said.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60746ae92cc1ef0018da138f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ashley Sorensen, with the 303rd Explosive Ordnance Disposal Battalion, attempts a new world record by running a mile in 11 minutes, 6 seconds, while wearing a fully functional bomb disposal suit\" height=\"2682\" width=\"4039\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Ashley Sorensen, with the 303rd Explosive Ordnance Disposal Battalion, attempts a new world record by running a mile in 11 minutes, 6 seconds, while wearing a fully functional bomb disposal suit.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Army</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The previous <a href=\"https://www.army.mil/article/112018/soldier_breaks_world_record_in_bomb_suit_run\">women&#39;s bomb suit mile run record was set by then-1st Lt. Ashley Sorenson, a friend of Hernandez in the EOD community, on Sept. 23, 2013</a> in Hawaii.</p><p>Sorenson &#34;was able to give me some advice - just to try and stay calm and remember it&#39;s only four more laps,&#34; Hernandez said. &#34;Once somebody put that in perspective, in my head I knew that I only had to run four more laps, and for the rest of my life it&#39;s done.&#34;</p><p>Hernandez&#39;s efforts were supported by the veteran-owned non-profit Headstrong, which provides mental health support for veterans and their families and backed Navy SEAL veteran Sean Matson&#39;s attempts to set a new men&#39;s bomb suit mile run record before a leg injury took him out of the competition.</p><p>The record for men, <a href=\"https://taskandpurpose.com/culture/bomb-suit-mile-world-record-kaitlyn-hernandez/\">as Task &#38; Purpose notes</a>, was set in 2017 by British Army soldier Mark Gibbs, who completed the run in 7 minutes and 24 seconds. He also ran a half-marathon in a full bomb suit, completing the event in 2 hours and 23 minutes.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.army.mil/article/245101/defusing_danger_soldier_sets_guinness_world_record\">Reflecting on her impressive run in discussions with the Army</a>, Hernandez said that &#34;as soon as it was done it was kind of a whirlwind, so I didn&#39;t really have a chance to take it in at first. But I was very happy and excited. The whole process has just been great.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:43:06","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:06","title":"What is Outlook Web App? A guide to Microsoft's web email service.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/outlook-web-app","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60709bfc4943790018bb1b12?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman at home working desktop computer typing\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>In addition to the desktop and mobile apps, Microsoft Outlook can be accessed in a browser with Outlook on the web.\n<p class=\"copyright\">PeopleImages/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Outlook Web App, also known as Outlook on the web, allows you to access your Outlook email account from a web browser.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">While Outlook on the web doesn&#39;t include all the features found in the desktop Outlook app, it&#39;s still convenient and useful.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">You can set up out of office messages, see your tasks and calendar, change your theme, and more when using Outlook in a web browser. </li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong>Visit Insider&#39;s Tech Reference library for more stories</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Outlook Web Access (OWA) is a browser-based way to access your <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/microsoft-outlook\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Microsoft Outlook</a> email. While it&#39;s also been known as Outlook Web App, it&#39;s now more commonly referred to as Outlook on the web. </p><p>OWA once applied exclusively to the online version of Outlook which came with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/microsoft-exchange\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Microsoft Exchange</a> Server. These days, Outlook on the web is more commonly accessed from a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-microsoft-365\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Microsoft 365</a> or free Outlook.com account.</p><p>While the version of Outlook that runs on your desktop as an app for <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/windows\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Windows</a> or <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/mac\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mac</a> still gives you the most flexibility, power, and features, you don&#39;t need to use it - Microsoft makes it easy to open your Outlook inbox in a web browser instead. That means you can see your Outlook inbox from any computer. </p><h2>How to open Outlook on the web</h2><p>To open Outlook on the web, just open the URL that&#39;s associated with your Outlook account. That should be the<a href=\"http://outlook.office.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> Microsoft 365 sign-in page</a> or, if you have a free Outlook account, <a href=\"https://outlook.live.com/owa/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Outlook.com</a>. Enter your email address and password and then select &#34;Sign in.&#34; </p><p>If you do happen to be using an Exchange Server rather than a Microsoft 365 account, you might need to ask your network administrator for the URL to the OWA website for your account. </p><h2>How to use Outlook on the web</h2><p>While Outlook on the web is a simplified version of Outlook, you&#39;ll probably still recognize it as the email program you already know from the desktop. Here&#39;s how to find your way around:</p><ul><li aria-level=\"1\">At the far left of the browser window is the folder list. It includes your Inbox, Sent items, and all the usual folders you have access to in Outlook. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">To the right of the folder list is the message list. This displays all the messages in the currently selected folder, and the selected message appears in the Reading pane on the right. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">You can also access additional features and settings from the toolbar at the top of the page and switch among Outlook&#39;s modes (Inbox, Calendar, To Do, and Contacts) using the array of icons at the bottom left of the page, under the folder list. </li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60707b944943790018bb1a33?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 1\" height=\"1518\" width=\"2023\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Outlook on the web displays your Outlook email in a web browser you can access from any computer.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><aside class=\"breakout-box headline-regular\"><h2><strong>How to compose a new message</strong></h2><ol><li aria-level=\"1\">Click &#34;New message&#34; at the top of the folder list. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">Start typing the name of the addressee in the &#34;To&#34; field. Outlook will display a dropdown menu of complete email addresses. Select the name from the list when it appears, or finish typing the email address from scratch. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">If you want to add a Cc or Bcc email, click it on the right side of the &#34;To&#34; field and fill in the email address. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">Add a subject line and then enter the body of your email message. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">To add an attachment, click &#34;Attach&#34; in the toolbar above the message window and then choose where the attachment is located from the dropdown menu. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">There are additional options available in the three-dot menu in the toolbar above the message window. Here you can save the message as a draft, add a signature, change the importance of the message, and more. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">When you&#39;re done, click &#34;Send.&#34;<br><br><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60707c54a451820019b3a479?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 2\" height=\"1515\" width=\"2026\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>After clicking &#34;New message,&#34; you can compose your email using an interface that should be relatively familiar.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></li></ol></aside><aside class=\"breakout-box headline-regular\"><h2><strong>How to set an out of office message</strong></h2><p>You&#39;re probably used to setting an &#34;out of office&#34; message when you&#39;re on vacation or otherwise unable to respond to new emails. You can set up an out of office message from the web.</p><ol><li aria-level=\"1\">Click the Settings icon (shaped like a gear) at the top right of the page and then, in the dropdown menu, click &#34;View all Outlook settings.&#34;<br><br><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60707d404943790018bb1a3d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 3\" height=\"1504\" width=\"2019\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Click &#34;View all Outlook settings&#34; to see more options, including the out of office controls.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></li><li aria-level=\"1\">On the Settings page, make sure you&#39;re on the &#34;Mail&#34; tab at the far left. </li><li aria-level=\"1\">Click &#34;Automatic replies&#34; in the middle pane.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">Turn on automatic replies by swiping the button to the right. Then compose the message and set the time frame you&#39;d like it to be active. Click &#34;Save&#34; when you&#39;re done.<br><br><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60707deb4943790018bb1a42?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 4\" height=\"1512\" width=\"2021\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Set your message and choose the time frame you&#39;d like it to run.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></li></ol><p>For more details, read our article on <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-set-out-of-office-in-outlook\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">how to set an &#34;Out of Office&#34; reply on Microsoft Outlook when you&#39;ll be unreachable by email</a>.</p></aside><h2>How to view your Outlook calendar</h2><p>To switch to the Outlook Calendar, just click the Calendar icon at the lower-left corner of the page. Here, you can customize the view. By default, you&#39;ll see the Month view, but click &#34;Month&#34; at the top-right and choose the view you prefer from the drop-down menu. </p><p>You can add events and appointments to your calendar using the &#34;New event&#34; button at the top-left of the page. For more tips on how to get the most out of your calendar, read our article on the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/outlook-calendar-tips-tricks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">best tips and tricks to manage your Outlook Calendar on any device</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60707e8f4943790018bb1a4b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 5\" height=\"1512\" width=\"2016\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Calendar can be opened from the icons at the lower-left corner of the webpage.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>How to manage your tasks and to dos</h2><p>To switch to your tasks, click the &#34;To Do&#34; icon at the lower-left corner of the page. If your left-most pane is too narrow, you might not see the icon; instead, click the three dots and then choose &#34;To Do&#34; from the pop-up menu. </p><p>The To Do page has a task list pane on the left side of the page and the list of tasks on the right. To create a task, click the list in which you want the task to appear. Then, in the task pane on the right, click to the right of the plus sign and type your to do. You can mark a task by creating it in the &#34;Important&#34; list or by clicking the star after creating it. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60707f384943790018bb1a4d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 6\" height=\"1513\" width=\"2023\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can just click the text field beside the plus sign and start typing to create new tasks.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>The best Outlook on the web settings</h2><p>While you can get up and running with Outlook on the web in minutes, there&#39;s a lot more power and customization hidden just under the surface. Here are some ways to get more out of Outlook on the web:</p><ul><li><strong>Filter your email</strong>. You can control what email is displayed and how it&#39;s sorted. At the top right of the message pane click &#34;Filter.&#34; In the dropdown menu, you can choose which messages you want to see - such as all messages, only unread, messages directly addressed to you, flagged messages, and so on. To change the sorting method, at the bottom of the dropdown menu choose &#34;Sort&#34; and select how you&#39;d like the messages to be organized. </li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60707fcf4943790018bb1a54?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 7\" height=\"1142\" width=\"1810\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Outlook on the web gives you a variety of sorting options.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Configure the reading pane.</strong> You can set the Reading pane to appear on the right of the message pane (which is the default), underneath the message pane, or you can even disable it entirely. Click the Settings icon (shaped like a gear) at the top-right of the page and, in the Reading pane section at the bottom of the page, choose &#34;Show on the right,&#34; &#34;Show on the bottom,&#34; or &#34;Hide.&#34; If you choose to hide the pane, messages will appear in a new window and take over the Outlook webpage when you click on a message in the message list. </li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607081aa4943790018bb1a61?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 8\" height=\"1516\" width=\"2029\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Reading pane can appear to the right or below the message list - or you can turn it off entirely.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Change your theme</strong>. Want a different theme for Outlook? Click the Settings icon (shaped like a gear) at the top right of the page and then choose a theme from the top of the Settings pane. There are more themes available than what you see here - click &#34;View all&#34; to see more. </li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607086444943790018bb1a8f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 9\" height=\"1504\" width=\"2042\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Use the Settings icon to change the visual theme of Outlook on the web.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Turn on dark mode</strong>. Dark mode is a popular feature that some people find easier on the eyes, especially in the evening hours.  Click the Settings icon (shaped like a gear) at the top right of the page and then and then turn on Dark mode by swiping the button to the right. </li><li><strong>Turn on desktop notifications</strong>. If you&#39;d like to see a pop-up notification about new messages even when your browser is not the focus of your desktop, you can turn on desktop notifications. Click the Settings icon (shaped like a gear) at the top right of the page and then turn on Desktop notifications by swiping the button to the right. In most cases, you&#39;ll also need to enable your browser to show notifications - look for a pop-up from your browser to enable these notifications. If you&#39;re using Chrome, for example, click &#34;Allow.&#34; In Firefox, click &#34;Allow Notifications.&#34;</li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607086c34943790018bb1a93?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 10\" height=\"1205\" width=\"2035\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>If you turn on notifications, be sure to enable notifications in the browser as well.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Customize display settings with display density</strong>. You can vary how many messages appear in the message list at once - you can pack them in more tightly or space them out, making them easier to browse. Click the Settings icon (shaped like a gear) at the top right of the page and find the Display density section. Choose &#34;Full,&#34; &#34;Medium,&#34; or &#34;Compact.&#34; Full is the most relaxed view and each message includes a small icon representing the sender. Medium removes the icon, which shrinks the size of each message slightly. Compact tightens up the spacing and puts the most messages on the page at once. </li><li><strong>View and group your conversations</strong>. You might be familiar with Outlook&#39;s Conversation view from the desktop version of the email app. Conversation view groups related emails together, making it easier to follow a conversation thread. You can control this setting in Outlook on the web as well. Click the Settings icon (shaped like a gear) at the top right of the page and find the Conversation view section. You can arrange your email so the newest replies in a conversation appear on top, appear on the bottom, or you can turn off conversation view entirely. If you do that, every message appears independently in the message pane, regardless of its relationship to other messages. </li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607087f04943790018bb1a9a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"What_is_Outlook_on_the_web 11\" height=\"1263\" width=\"2036\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You have several options for configuring how to group and view messages in Outlook on the web.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dave Johnson/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module-end-of-article\" 00:43:06","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:06","title":"Elon Musk asked Cathie Wood about the Buffett indicator flashing red. The Ark Invest chief is taking a closer look.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-cathie-wood-warren-buffett-indicator-analysis-stock-market-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60350902bed5c50011a2c023?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GettyImages 1229892852\" height=\"512\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Elon Musk.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Britta Pedersen-Pool/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>Elon Musk asked Cathie Wood about the Buffett indicator&#39;s record level.</strong></li><li><strong>The Ark Invest chief said it was relatively low and justified by new technologies.</strong></li><li><strong>Critics say stocks are far more expensive now than they were in the late 1800s.</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>Elon Musk <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/elon-musk-cathie-wood-ark-warren-buffett-indicator-not-worried-2021-4-1030277873\">recently asked</a> Cathie Wood for her view on Warren Buffett&#39;s favorite indicator, which has surged to a record 200% and may be <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-indicator-record-high-overvalued-stock-market-crash-2021-2-1030067388\">signaling a stock-market crash</a> around the corner.</p><p>The Ark Invest chief initially dismissed the gauge as outdated but told the Tesla boss on Sunday that her team would analyze it.</p><p>&#34;@ARKInvest will research this metric pre-WWII to assess its validity,&#34; Wood <a href=\"https://twitter.com/CathieDWood/status/1381230151070056451\">tweeted</a>.</p><p>The star stock-picker disclosed the plan after suggesting that the Buffett indicator had reached double or triple its current level in the late 1800s. Transformative technologies such as the telephone, electricity, and the automobile sent the gauge skyward, she explained, adding that modern innovations such as robotics, blockchain, and artificial intelligence are far more revolutionary in her book.</p><p>&#34;&#39;This time is different&#39; are dangerous words in forecasting markets,&#34; Wood said, before doubling down on her view that the Buffett indicator is relatively low and that disruptive technologies justify its elevated level.</p><p>Chris Bloomstran, the head of Semper Augustus Investments, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ChrisBloomstran/status/1381358671070912512\">swiftly rebutted her comments</a>. The US stock market peaked at 90% of national GDP in 1929, he said, highlighting that public companies generated a far smaller proportion of economic output back then and that global trade was a fraction of its current level.</p><p>Moreover, Bloomstran argued that Wood&#39;s vaunted technologies &#34;will not be remotely more transformative than those from 1870 to the 1950s.&#34; He pointed out that, despite the innovations she outlined, the US stock market plummeted almost 90% during the Great Depression.</p><p>The so-called Buffett indicator takes the total market capitalization of a country&#39;s publicly traded stocks and divides it by the latest quarterly GDP figure available. Based on the Wilshire 5000 Total Market Index&#39;s level of $43.3 trillion and the latest estimate for fourth-quarter US GDP of $21.5 trillion, the yardstick has reached about 201%.</p><p>Buffett described his namesake gauge in 2001 as &#34;probably the best single measure of where valuations stand at any given moment.&#34; It should have been a &#34;very strong warning signal&#34; of a crash when it skyrocketed during the dot-com boom, he added.</p><p>Now the indicator has soared to new heights, it&#39;s no surprise to see Musk&#39;s querying someone like Wood on whether he should be worried and Wood&#39;s deciding to take a closer look.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/real-estate-stock-picks-strong-pricing-power-rising-rates-bofa-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">BANK OF AMERICA: Buy these 7 real-estate stocks with cast-iron balance sheets and strong pricing power that look poised to soar even as rates rise</a></em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-cathie-wood-warren-buffett-indicator-analysis-stock-market-2021-4'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:V_sGLiPBpWU\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:qj6IDK7rITs\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:gIN9vFwOqvQ\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:gIN9vFwOqvQ\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/9RGAU4C7LmM\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Apr 2021 16:32:38 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/60742add3e3fe7001882a0fc?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"6e7fcccbe0a9aa49b32e1f3be4b16647","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn36@2020_4/2021/04/12/16-44-10-626_3a1b284096024168.webp","destWidth":900,"destHeight":675,"sourceBytes":35048,"destBytes":35048,"author":"tmohamed@businessinsider.com (Theron Mohamed)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60350902bed5c50011a2c023?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn15@2020_5/2021/04/12/16-44-14-289_d1c2bcef17a1b173.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn39@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-44-16-326_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn25@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-44-15-275_297b8fa26e53baf8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn14@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-44-15-801_b51ecddceebfc15a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn51@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-44-13-888_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=9RGAU4C7LmM:cXhDgCjopOo:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn10@2020_6/2021/04/12/16-44-15-212_44d082f12d7f2b4f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/9RGAU4C7LmM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn40@2020_3/2021/04/12/16-44-14-354_90e738e2dfbb1fce.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1618245786383},{"createdTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:06","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:06","title":"It's now or never for Democrats: either pass H.R. 1 or watch voter suppression bills like Georgia's become the norm","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/democrats-pass-hr-1-elections-voting-rights-suppression-georgia-congress-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606f7f954d3e410018b70224?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Georgia voting\" height=\"992\" width=\"1985\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A person with voter protection waits for voters to arrive during Georgia&#39;s Senate runoff elections on Tuesday, Jan. 5, 2021, in Atlanta.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brynn Anderson/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>Georgia&#39;s restrictive SB 202 bill is merely a warning shot.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>There are currently more than 360 bills in 47 state legislatures restricting access to voting.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Democrats have a limited window of opportunity to pass landmark voting rights legislation before losing their majorities.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Carl Gibson is a freelance journalist and columnist from Kentucky.</strong></li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Georgia&#39;s Senate Bill 202 is by far the most draconian law passed by any state legislature with respect to restricting access to voting. This is merely an opening salvo in a widespread assault on the right to vote, and other Republican-controlled state legislatures are hoping to pass similar bills. The only way to head off the wave of attacks on the fundamental right of all citizens to have equal access to vote is for Democrats to use their slim majorities to immediately pass new voter protections. If HR 1 (<a href=\"https://www.congress.gov/bill/117th-congress/house-bill/1/text\">the For The People Act</a>) and the <a href=\"https://www.congress.gov/bill/116th-congress/house-bill/4/text\">John Lewis Voting Rights Advancement Act</a> don&#39;t become law, Georgia&#39;s anti-voting law will become just one of many.</p><h2>Republicans are moving the goal-post </h2><p>A New York Times analysis of the new Georgia elections law (SB 202) found that, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/02/us/politics/georgia-voting-law-annotated.html\">among other things</a>, it limits the window of time to request an absentee ballot, makes it illegal for election officials to mail absentee ballots to all voters, levies criminal penalties for anyone who gives water to voters in long lines, severely limits the number of ballot drop boxes, and replaces the secretary of state as chair of the State Election Board with someone elected from the state legislature. The Georgia legislature (which has been under Republican control <a href=\"https://ballotpedia.org/Party_control_of_Georgia_state_government\">since 2005</a>) also now has the power to remove municipal and county election officials and replace them with people appointed by partisan state lawmakers. </p><p>Georgia Governor Brian Kemp (R) has <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2021/03/25/981357583/georgia-legislature-approves-election-overhaul-including-changes-to-absentee-vot\">argued</a> the new law is necessary to make the state&#39;s elections &#34;secure, accessible, and fair.&#34; This is despite Georgia&#39;s Republican Secretary of State, Brad Raffensperger, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/2020/11/21/brad-raffensperger-georgia-results-2020-election-trustworthy/\">stating in a Washington Post op-ed</a> that &#34;Georgia&#39;s voting system has never been more secure or trustworthy.&#34; Even Georgia Lieutenant Governor Geoff Duncan (R) <a href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/entertainment/kemp-deputy-expresses-concerns-about-georgias-new-voting-law-there-were-some-things-i-didnt-like-214143449.html?guccounter=1&guce_referrer=aHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuZ29vZ2xlLmNvbS8&guce_referrer_sig=AQAAALoc0xScjRXSOrL3zk-riewIMpEYIdxcCmaBpJdTBvoFGdXdv8XMDGRG7TGAxVxphmhNcqvE2YMkuKjNKGK-4rw4CQoEAJc8SR2zicTt4Je0u3_IOFErg97ovymX2BsEv86-BcgzVeAHhjKMriNNV7EsioLl6_P6PvpCj8Q_NpERj8Q_NpER\">thought the bill went too far</a> to curb access to voting. </p><p>Various civil rights groups have since <a href=\"https://www.ajc.com/politics/politics-blog/georgias-sweeping-elections-overhaul-faces-new-legal-challenge/ARLWEI7SENEKNC4VUGWSHGGUIA/\">filed a legal challenge</a> to SB 202, petitioning for the law to be rendered unconstitutional and in violation of the Voting Rights Act. But because Georgia is part of the 11th Circuit Court of Appeals, and because a majority of the circuit&#39;s judges were <a href=\"https://www.ca11.uscourts.gov/eleventh-circuit-judges\">appointed by Republican presidents</a>, SB 202 may very well be upheld. Even if the 11th Circuit struck down the law, appellants could end up swaying the United States Supreme Court, which maintains a 6-3 conservative majority. Moreover, Chief Justice John Roberts even <a href=\"https://www.oyez.org/cases/2012/12-96\">wrote the majority opinion</a> in the landmark voting rights case that opened the door for bills like SB 202 to become law across the country. </p><p>The 2013 <em>Shelby County vs. Holder</em> decision will undoubtedly be remembered in history books with the same level of disdain as the 1857 <em>Dred Scott vs. Sandford</em> decision. Both decisions created false racial hierarchies rendering Black people to second-class citizen status. Whereas <em>Dred Scott</em> declared Black people did not have the rights of citizenship, <em>Shelby County</em> declared that the portion of the Voting Rights Act of 1965 pertaining to protections for Black voters <a href=\"https://www.scotusblog.com/case-files/cases/shelby-county-v-holder/\">was unconstitutional</a>. This released <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2019/6/25/18701277/shelby-county-v-holder-anniversary-voting-rights-suppression-congress\">nine mostly Southern states</a> - Alabama, Alaska, Arizona, Georgia, Louisiana, Mississippi, South Carolina, Texas, and Virginia - from getting &#34;pre-clearance&#34; from the federal judiciary before changing laws pertaining to voting rights. At the time, Justice Antonin Scalia justified his vote to eliminate those protections by saying the Voting Rights Act created &#34;<a href=\"https://www.newyorker.com/news/amy-davidson/in-voting-rights-scalia-sees-a-racial-entitlement\">racial entitlement</a>&#34; for Black voters. </p><p>Just days after the <em>Shelby County</em> decision, the League of Women Voters warned that &#34;<a href=\"https://www.lwv.org/blog/supreme-court-ruling-opens-door-widespread-voter-suppression\">the floodgates have opened</a>&#34; for widespread voter suppression legislation across the country and called for Congress to pass legislation guaranteeing everyone the right to vote. They were right: according to the Brennan Center for Justice, there are <a href=\"https://www.brennancenter.org/our-work/research-reports/voting-laws-roundup-march-2021\">at least 361 bills</a> awaiting action in 47 states that aim to curtail ballot access for voters. Five of those bills have already become law this year, and 29 bills have been passed by at least one legislative chamber. 49 of those bills are in Texas. And in Arizona and Georgia - states with Republican-controlled legislatures where Joe Biden narrowly defeated Donald Trump in the 2020 election - there are 23 and 25 pending voter suppression bills, respectively.</p><h2>For Democrats, it&#39;s now or never</h2><p>The best way to beat back this wave of anti-voting bills is to pass federal legislation guaranteeing the absolute right of all citizens to cast a ballot. HR 1, which <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/03/politics/house-democrats-hr1-vote/index.html\">passed the House in March</a> and is currently awaiting action in the Senate, would go a long way toward advancing that goal. Among other things, the bill would establish automatic voter registration, in which citizens are automatically registered on their state&#39;s voter rolls when getting state-issued driver&#39;s licenses and ID cards. It would also guarantee same-day voter registration for federal elections, which allows citizens to register to vote at their polling precinct on the day of the election. HR 1 also requires states to open up the early voting period at least two weeks before an election. </p><p>The John Lewis Voting Rights Advancement Act, which was introduced in the Senate in the 116th Congress, is the perfect companion to HR 1. That bill restores the preclearance requirement in the Voting Rights Act that was undone by the <em>Shelby County</em> decision, forcing state governments to win approval from the federal bench before changing election laws. The Act also broadens cases in which the Department of Justice can send federal election observers to states that federal courts have deemed necessary to ensure adequate protections are in place for all voters. </p><p>While these bills are great antidotes for the wave of voter suppression bills being introduced across the country, they still have yet to overcome the key hurdle of the filibuster. Even though they don&#39;t control the Senate, Republicans can still invoke the filibuster for any non-budgetary legislation, requiring an impenetrable 60-vote threshold first be met before a bill can even get an up-or-down vote. If they had a unified bloc, Democrats could make procedural maneuvers to eliminate the filibuster with Vice President Kamala Harris casting the tie-breaking vote. Centrist Democrat senators like Joe Manchin and Kyrsten Sinema are still currently in favor of keeping the filibuster, dooming voting rights legislation to the legislative graveyard. However, President Joe Biden may be warming to the idea of limiting the power of the filibuster and could even be making moves behind the scenes to eliminate it entirely.</p><p>Biden has also notably <a href=\"https://twitter.com/dlippman/status/1375430289313398788\">appointed Gayle Manchin</a>, Joe Manchin&#39;s wife, to a &#34;key position&#34; in the White House, essentially tying Manchin&#39;s family to his administration. It&#39;s difficult to see how this isn&#39;t a maneuver to placate Manchin in an effort to soften the senator&#39;s position on the filibuster (admittedly a tall order given Manchin&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/joe-manchin-filibuster-vote/2021/04/07/cdbd53c6-97da-11eb-a6d0-13d207aadb78_story.html\">recent op-ed</a> in favor of keeping it). In the event Manchin does eventually flip on the filibuster, Sinema could soon follow, not wanting to be seen as the lone obstacle in the way of significant voting rights expansion.</p><p>If Senate Democrats act to eliminate the filibuster, it should be done right away. As The Daily Poster <a href=\"https://www.dailyposter.com/p/dems-could-lose-their-majority-at?token=eyJ1c2VyX2lkIjo0MjMxMzQ1LCJwb3N0X2lkIjozNDI4NTMxMywiXyI6Ijc3cTE5IiwiaWF0IjoxNjE2Nzc3MzM1LCJleHAiOjE2MTY3ODA5MzUsImlzcyI6InB1Yi0zNzc3OCIsInN1YiI6InBvc3QtcmVhY3Rpb24ifQ.cSuGIvQ34ytv70KlF_ipe_coSrpBo6dUElBcOU6YdUc\">recently pointed out</a>, there are multiple septuagenarian senators from states with Republican governors. Should anything happen to aging senators like Patrick Leahy, Ed Markey, Bernie Sanders, or Elizabeth Warren, any one of them could be replaced with a Republican, abruptly ending Democrats&#39; control of the Senate and putting Senate Minority Leader Mitch McConnell back in the driver&#39;s seat.</p><p>Democrats will have to decide relatively soon whether they&#39;d rather keep a Jim Crow relic like the filibuster, or have new federal voting rights legislation. If they want any hope of stopping the relentless march of state-level, Republican-led voter suppression efforts, it&#39;s obvious what must be done: Democrats should immediately nuke the filibuster and pass HR 1 and the John Lewis Voting Rights Advancement Act, or kiss their majorities goodbye.</p><p><em>Carl Gibson is a freelance journalist whose work has been published in CNN, The Guardian, The Washington Post, The Houston Chronicle, Barron&#39;s, The Independent, and NPR, among others. Follow him on Twitter </em><a href=\"http://twitter.com/crgibs\"><em>@crgibs</em></a><em>.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=alza9vZJa-w:dKrOcfBW-3U:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/alza9vZJa-w\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 12 Apr 2021 13:04:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/606f7f924d3e410018b70223?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"8c44dcb983b2fdc207af4b55996ea26b","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn51@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-44-10-958_b68150faee48f670.webp","destWidth":1778,"destHeight":1333,"sourceBytes":57378,"destBytes":57378,"author":"insider@insider.com (Carl Gibson)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/606f7f954d3e410018b70224?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn44@2020_1/2021/04/12/16-44-12-589_4047b62a67b27d4f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn39@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-44-16-326_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=alza9vZJa-w:dKrOcfBW-3U:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn74@2020_5/2021/04/12/16-44-15-520_6286a5da0787ebd6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=alza9vZJa-w:dKrOcfBW-3U:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn92@2020_3/2021/04/12/16-44-15-113_0c8749ebc609a537.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn51@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-44-13-888_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=alza9vZJa-w:dKrOcfBW-3U:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn10@2020_2/2021/04/12/16-44-17-789_198b8561f2da9968.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/alza9vZJa-w":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn51@2020_5/2021/04/12/16-44-11-939_1ee35fba662a8908.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1618245786457},{"createdTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:06","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:06","title":"Voting laws in states like Georgia are getting a lot of attention, but New York City is also failing to secure the right to vote for some of its most marginalized citizens","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-voting-rights-prisoners-nyc-department-corrections-board-elections-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606f8ca230004b0019b26c86?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rikers island NYC prison\" height=\"933\" width=\"1866\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A sign marks the location of the Rikers Correctional Center in the East River on March 9, 2021 in New York City.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gary Hershorn/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Recently a slew of Republican-held states, like Georgia, have passed or are considering restrictive voting laws.</li>\n<li>But there are also issues in New York City, where prisoners must rely on the effectiveness of prison staff to secure their votes.</li>\n<li>There are a number of things Bill de Blasio and his colleagues can do to ensure that prisoners get a chance to vote.</li>\n<li>Ashish Prashar is the Global Chief Marketing Officer at R/GA and a justice reform activist.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Jim Crow remains alive and all too well among voters in Georgia, Florida, and yes, in New York City, where the most diverse field ever to seek the mayor&#39;s office is preparing for a June primary. </p><p>You know about the recent news from Georgia. On March 25, Georgia Governor Brian Kemp signed a law pushed through by state Republicans. Among other things, the law <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/georgia-voting-restrictions/2021/03/25/91009e72-8da1-11eb-9423-04079921c915_story.html\">strips some of the power to run Georgia elections</a> from the secretary of state and local counties and transfers oversight to a state board that conservatives likely will dominate. The law infamously includes <a href=\"https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/kemp-sign-sweeping-elections-bill-passed-georgia-legislature/story?id=76677927\">a ban on providing food and water to people waiting in line to vote</a>. Gov. Kemp justified the law, citing <a href=\"https://www.usnews.com/news/politics/articles/2021-03-25/georgia-house-passes-gop-election-bill-despite-criticism\">dubious questions about whether the 2020 election in Georgia was fair</a>. </p><p>You also likely know the challenges placed on voters in Florida. In the run up to the 2020 elections, State Republicans, led by Gov. Ron DeSantis, erected a huge barrier to the state&#39;s amendment granting voting rights to people with felony records. The amendment was approved by 64% of voters. Republicans inserted a poll tax requirement to the amendment that required those with felony records to <a href=\"https://www.clickorlando.com/news/politics/2020/09/11/florida-felons-cant-vote-until-they-pay-fines-judge-rules/\">pay all fines and fees</a> from their sentence before they could vote. </p><p>However, you likely don&#39;t know the challenges that New York City voters have. In New York, a diverse, global, and decidedly liberal city, people in pre-trial detention are free to vote. However, as the June 22 primary nears, featuring dozens of candidates representing the city&#39;s diversity, the New York Department of Corrections is <a href=\"https://gothamist.com/news/city-ignoring-mandate-informing-a-detainees-right-to-vote-legal-advocates-say\">not meeting its obligations to voting access in NYC jails</a>. The overwhelming majority of people have not received voter registration information, there are no posters or signs with voter information, and people have not received voter registration education. The failure to take these steps only increases the barriers to voting among this population.</p><p>The New York City Charter requires DOC to implement a program to assist individuals with voting. Because people in NYC jails are required to vote by absentee ballot, they must rely entirely on DOC staff to exercise their right to vote. More importantly, a loophole in the registration rules further disenfranchises some people in NYC jails. For the upcoming election, the last day to postmark an application for an absentee ballot is June 15 and the last day to postmark an absentee ballot is June 22. This means eligible voters admitted into DOC custody after June 15 and held through June 22 won&#39;t be able to vote.</p><p>In order to ensure all New Yorkers can vote, Mayor Bill de Blasio, Deputy Mayor Phillip Thompson, Executive Director Margaret Egan, Commissioner Andrew Spano, and Commissioner Cynthia Brann must listen to <a href=\"https://legalaidnyc.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/04-02-21-LAS-and-35-Organizations-Call-for-Greater-Access-to-Voter-Registration-in-NYC-Jails.pdf\">the Legal Aid Society</a> and ensure eligible voters in New York City jails have prompt and secure ballot access without hindrance. In order to accomplish this, they must:</p><ul><li aria-level=\"1\">Provide a report on what steps have been taken to implement the voting policy in New York City jails announced last year at the September Board of Corrections (BOC) meeting.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">Show that the BOC works with the DOC and the Board of Elections (BOE) to get &#34;emergency&#34; poll sites set up in every jail, and allows every eligible incarcerated person to i) register, and ii) vote by affidavit on election day.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">Prove that the BOC requests from both the DOC and the BOE to report the number of eligible voters in DOC custody, the number of registration forms they received, the number of registration forms they considered valid, the number of absentee ballot applications they received and accepted as valid, and the number of absentee ballots received and accepted as valid. </li></ul><p>There is an incredible amount of confusion and misinformation surrounding access to voting that systematically deprives people the right to vote. Ensuring appropriate accommodations for all voters - South and North of the Mason-Dixon Line, in jail or free - is the crucial first step in protecting a fundamental right to our democracy.</p><p><em>Ashish Prashar is the Global CMO at R/GA and a justice reform activist. He sits on the board of Exodus Transitional Community, Getting Out and Staying Out, Just Leadership, Leap Confronting Conflict and the Responsible Business Initiative for Justice. @Ash_Prashar</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/60205b3e67d1e300113c4b50?format=jpeg\" alt=\"astrazeneca vaccine\" height=\"1312\" width=\"1749\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A vial and syringe in front of the AstraZeneca logo.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters/Dado Ruvic</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Up to 80% of Sicilians are rejecting the AstraZeneca jab, the leader of the region has said. </li>\n<li>Italy is using the shot, but has advised that it be avoided in younger age groups.</li>\n<li>Fears, based on rare blood clots, are &#34;understandable, but unjustified,&#34; a top Sicily are turning down the AstraZeneca vaccine when it is offered, the island&#39;s leader said on Saturday. </p><p>Nello Musumeci, Sicily&#39;s president said in a press conference on Saturday that &#34;out of 100 people, 80 say no&#34; to the AstraZeneca vaccine, <a href=\"https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20210411-up-to-80-percent-in-sicily-refuse-az-vaccine-president\">AFP reported</a>.</p><p>A spokesperson for Musumeci later told AFP that the figure was too extreme and that he had meant to say &#34;up to 80%.&#34;</p><p>In some cities, like Syracuse, the refusal rate was lower, around 30%, the spokesperson said.</p><p>Musumeci said that he understood why people would be concerned about the vaccine, but that Sicilians &#34;have a duty to believe scientists&#34; when they say the vaccine is safe, <a href=\"https://gds.it/articoli/politica/2021/04/11/vaccini-musumeci-avverte-in-sicilia-l80-dice-no-ad-astrazeneca-df8ac640-37e8-4404-b13e-84bd78eb04f4/?utm_medium=feed&utm_source=twitter.com&utm_campaign=Feed%3A+gds_twitter_feedter_feed\">Giornale di Sicilia reported</a>.</p><p>&#34;The only solution is to immunize the Sicilian community,&#34; he said.</p><p>The European Medicines Agency (EMA) last week listed unusual blood clots with low platelets <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/author/catherine-schuster-bruce\">as a very rare side effect</a> of the AstraZeneca vaccine. The agency said that the benefits of the shot outweigh the risks. </p><p>The Italian government has said that <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/health-coronavirus-italy-astrazeneca/italy-recommends-astrazeneca-covid-vaccine-only-for-over-60s-idUSR1N2LL03R\">the AstraZeneca vaccine should be avoided</a> by those under the age of 60, but that &#34;anyone who wants to be vaccinated with AstraZeneca can continue to be.&#34;</p><p>The fear about the vaccine are &#34;understandable, but unjustified,&#34; said government advisor Franco Locatelli on Sunday, <a href=\"https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20210411-up-to-80-percent-in-sicily-refuse-az-vaccine-president\">AFP reported</a>.</p><p>&#34;I say that we are offering a vaccine that is safe and effective, which people must accept,&#34; he said to the La Stampa newspaper.</p><p>&#34;That said, if we find ourselves facing a disarming number of defections, we will reconsider the issue.&#34;</p><p>Italy has been struggling to get its COVID-19 outbreak under control and its vaccination campaign has been criticized for being sluggish <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/europe/italy-vaccines-death-toll/2021/04/08/2d621f12-971a-11eb-8f0a-3384cf4fb399_story.html\">The Washington Post reported</a>.</p><p>Unlikely other European countries, which have seen a downtick in the number of deaths, Italy&#39;s death rate has remained high.</p><p>The country now has the seventh-highest death toll of COVID-19, with over <a href=\"https://ourworldindata.org/covid-deaths\">113,000 COVID-19 deaths as of April 11</a>. <a href=\"https://www.prb.org/countries-with-the-oldest-populations/\">22% of its population is over the age of 65</a>, which gives it the second-oldest population of any country.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/astrazeneca-covid-19-vaccine-no-evidence-to-stop-use-ema-2021-3\">Germany, France</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/under-30s-shouldnt-take-astrazeneca-vaccine-uk-regulator-2021-4\">the UK</a>, and other countries have restricted the use of the vaccine in younger people over concerns about unusual blood clots. </p><p>Experts have told Insider that having the shot is still safe and is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/astrazeneca-vaccine-worth-it-despite-blood-clot-link-experts-2021-4\">less risky than flying in a plane</a>. One expert told Insider that the real risk was that vaccine skepticism would rise among those who are offered the vaccine. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:43:06","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:06","title":"How Dwight D. Eisenhower 'lost' a B-17 bomber in a bet with a British general","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-dwight-d-eisenhower-lost-a-b17-bomber-in-bet-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5dd49944fd9db24aae76ad05?format=jpeg\" alt=\"b-17 b 17 E big ass\" height=\"600\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A B-17 bomber.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:B-17E#/media/File:Color_Photographed_B-17E_in_Flight.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">US Air Force</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>In late 1942 and early 1943, the Allies were scrambling to defeat the Germans in North Africa.</li>\n<li>Gen. Dwight D. Eisenhower wanted his forces to move faster, leading to an unusual deal with British Lt. Gen. Bernard Montgomery.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The liberation of Sfax, Tunisia on April 10, 1943 was a joyous occasion for nearly everyone involved.</p><p>The Allies gained an important Mediterranean port, the Tunisians in the city were liberated, and British Lt. Gen. Bernard Montgomery won a B-17 bomber from Gen. Dwight D. Eisenhower.</p><p>That last one may need some explanation.</p><h2>Rommel retreats to the Mareth line</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cf937e411e2054e490d9744?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Gen. Bernard &#34;Monty&#34; Montgomery addresses British troops\" height=\"2260\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Gen. Bernard Montgomery addressing British troops.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Montgomery had been fighting German Field Marshal Erwin Rommel for months in North Africa. Though the campaign was slowly succeeding, Rommel and his Italian allies were inflicting heavy casualties on the British.</p><p>Britain wanted to increase forces in North Africa to keep Rommel off-balance. Meanwhile, the other Allied nations wanted to capture North Africa so they could begin invading Italy from the south.</p><p>So in late October 1942, Montgomery launched Operation Lightfoot. British tanks and other forces moved under cover of massive artillery barrages through minefields against dug-in German positions. By November 2, Rommel was in a rapid withdrawal east, sacrificing troops by the hundreds to try and keep his lines of retreat open.</p><p>This put the German units in disarray when Operation Torch was launched on Nov. 8. More than <a href=\"http://www.historylearningsite.co.uk/world-war-two/war-in-north-africa/operation-torch/\">73,000 troops</a> landed along the north coast of Africa in a deliberate attempt to squeeze the Axis east.</p><p>It worked, but Germany and Italy still held Tunisia and conducted their own surge, <a href=\"https://books.google.com/books?id=oD9Z3omHy3ICpg=PA450lpg=PA450dq=Sfax+tunisia+captured+World+War+IIsource=blots=C-zz1S6jzlsig=E_DGC8Vq3iUdkQrX4axTPgsRO6Ihl=ensa=Xei=f_yJVZy1JdKyoQSp-rjoBgved=0CEcQ6AEwBg#v=onepageq=Sfaxf=false\">landing nearly 250,000 troops in and around the ports at Mareth and Sfax</a>. They would settle into a defense along <a href=\"http://www.thewarillustrated.info/153/how-montgomery-captured-the-mareth-line.asp\">the Mareth Line</a>.</p><h2>The bet is made</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/564342ac9dd7cc1d008c9096?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Patton hewitt ww2 world war ii north africa\" height=\"580\" width=\"840\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Maj. Gen. George S. Patton, left, aboard USS Augusta off North Africa in 1942.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Pattonhewitt.jpg#/media/File:Pattonhewitt.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">US Navy Photograph</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The battles in North Africa raged back and forth as German reinforcements tried to hold the line.</p><p>The Allied forces were slowly gaining ground, with <a href=\"http://www.wearethemighty.com/video/gen-patton-battles-throws-woes-mid-life-crisis-patton-present-pt-1\">Maj. Gen. George S. Patton</a> and Montgomery both attempting to be the first to capture key cities, but Eisenhower wanted them to move faster.</p><p>Eisenhower&#39;s chief of staff, Maj. Gen. Bedell Smith, was visiting Montgomery at his headquarters in the spring of 1943.</p><p>Exact accounts of the conversation vary, but Montgomery asked about getting a B-17 for his personal use. Smith told Montgomery that if Montgomery captured Sfax by April 15, Eisenhower would give him whatever he wanted.</p><p>Smith reportedly meant it as a joke wager, but the notorious gambler Montgomery was serious.</p><h2>Sfax falls and Montgomery gets his B-17</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607452523e3fe7001882a14c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"B 17C with RAF colors\" height=\"787\" width=\"1050\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A B-17 with RAF colors.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Boeing_Fortress_in_British_service#/media/File:B-17C_with_RAF_colors.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">US Air Force</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>On April 10 - five days ahead of the deadline - Montgomery captured Sfax and immediately asked for payment.</p><p>Eisenhower honored the bet and sent Montgomery a <a href=\"http://www.gettyimages.com/detail/video/general-bernard-law-montgomery-wins-a-bet-against-news-footage/504249711\">B-17 bomber and crew</a> even though the bombers were needed for the war effort.</p><p>The event caused a strain between <a href=\"https://books.google.com/books?id=RCeteK7LEiYCpg=PA411lpg=PA411dq=Montgomery+B-17+betsource=blots=an36GixR1Xsig=uvcBqS6HYp_9eeNzFBhM57SjsL8hl=ensa=Xei=NFeIVZSMFITuoATA3KI4ved=0CCQQ6AEwAQ#v=onepageq=Montgomery%20B-17%20betf=false\">Eisenhower and Montgomery</a> as well as between Eisenhower and Patton.</p><p>Patton was incensed that a British general had a personal B-17 while he was struggling for rides or moving in convoys. Eisenhower was angry that Montgomery would actually accept a B-17 when they were needed to actually bomb targets.</p><p>Eisenhower mentioned it to Montgomery&#39;s boss, Sir Alan Brooke, who berated Montgomery for crass stupidity. The plane was written off after a crash-landing a month later and never replaced.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 00:43:06","updatedTime":"2021-04-13 00:43:06","title":"Elon Musk tweeted then deleted an anti-vaccine cartoon featuring Bill Gates. Here's where their simmering feud began and how it's escalated amid the pandemic.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-bill-gates-feud-coronavirus-electric-cars-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f73623974fe5b0018a8dfd1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Elon Musk Bill Gates\" height=\"1920\" width=\"2560\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Elon Musk and Bill Gates.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Susan Walsh/AP; Mike Cohen/Getty Images for The New York Times</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Elon Musk-Bill Gates feud dates back to early 2020 when Gates commented on electric cars.</li>\n<li>The two moguls appear to fundamentally disagree about the coronavirus as well. </li>\n<li>In April, Musk tweeted and deleted an anti-vaccine cartoon featuring Gates.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider&#39;s homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Bill Gates and Elon Musk don&#39;t exactly see eye to eye.</p><p>While the Microsoft billionaire and the Tesla and SpaceX titan have never had a particularly cozy relationship, things have heated up over the past year as the two have openly sparred about everything from electric vehicles to the coronavirus.</p><p>The two moguls are <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/billionaires/?sref=BWbpWjRm\">among the world&#39;s wealthiest</a>, eclipsed only by Amazon CEO Jeff Bezos. While their public spats may not always be serious, they do appear to fundamentally disagree about the coronavirus - and as major players in virus treatment and the vaccine to protect against it, their clashes carry even more weight.</p><p>Here&#39;s where the friction between Gates and Musk began and everything that&#39;s happened since.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tGates doesn't appear to be a fan of Tesla vehicles, and he's said as much publicly.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f73675c74fe5b0018a8dfed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bill Gates\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bill Gates.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Elaine Thompson/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In February 2020, Gates said during <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FV2tMP37ygs\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"de80cf0020c2612fa1954ea96c837070\">an interview with the YouTuber Marques Brownlee</a> that while Tesla had helped to drive innovation and adoption of electric vehicles, he recently bought a Porsche Taycan.</p>\n\tGates' comments didn't get by Musk, who tweeted that his conversations with Gates had always been \"underwhelming.\"\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f6baf60e3e7670011716301?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Elon Musk\" height=\"1763\" width=\"2350\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Elon Musk.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Odd Andersen/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><em>Source: <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1229568241552502784?s=20\">Elon Musk/Twitter</a></em></p>\n\tBut things really heated up in July when Gates took issue with Musk's comments on the coronavirus pandemic.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7368ba74fe5b0018a8dff3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bill Gates \" height=\"2423\" width=\"3231\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bill Gates.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In an <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/07/28/bill-gates-lies-spread-faster-than-facts-on-social-media.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"dbf08c0d7609374e9afd075e4b6c932b\">interview on CNBC's \"Squawk Box,\"</a> Gates criticized Musk's comments on the virus and implied that Musk shouldn't be speaking about the pandemic at all.</p><p>\"Elon's positioning is to maintain a high level of outrageous comments,\" Gates said. \"He's not much involved in vaccines. He makes a great electric car. And his rockets work well. So he's allowed to say these things. I hope that he doesn't confuse areas he's not involved in too much.\"</p><p>Gates and Musk are involved in fighting the coronavirus, with Gates <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-bill-gates-is-dealing-with-coronavirus-outbreak-2020\">pledging $100 million to fight the virus</a> via the Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation and Musk redirecting Tesla resources to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-ventilator-controversy-explained-2020-4\">source and produce ventilators</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-building-microfactories-with-coronavirus-vaccine-maker-curevac-2020-7\">teaming up with the German biotech firm CureVac</a> &#8212; in which <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/08/17/investing/curevac-vaccine-stock/index.html\">Gates is an investor</a> &#8212; to make a device to aid in vaccine production.</p><p>But since last March, Musk has frequently downplayed the severity of the virus and strongly criticized stay-at-home orders. He's <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-coronavirus-comments-timeline-stay-at-home-rules-fascist-2020-5#musk-plugs-the-malaria-drug-chloroquine-a-possible-covid-19-treatment-which-is-not-scientifically-proven-4\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"0887536f5334084d484ad160243c38ca\">promoted the malaria drug hydroxychloroquine</a> as a treatment for the virus, falsely said that children are immune to it, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-coronavirus-death-counts-lie-too-high-2020-5\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"8c30b1d5f3c140fd096c8c7551696103\">questioned coronavirus-deaths data</a>.</p><p>Musk also said last year that there would be \"<a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1240754657263144960\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"92475f6fe3d502a0f337a1bb6761e3c2\">close to zero new cases</a>\" by the end of April 2020. The death toll in the US alone recently surpassed 500,000.</p>\n\tThe comments struck a nerve with Musk, who taunted Gates on Twitter.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f73698a0ab50d00184ad0a0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"elon musk\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Elon Musk.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Win McNamee/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Musk jokingly posted multiple tweets about Gates, including \"Billy G is not my lover\" and \"The rumor that Bill Gates &#38; I are lovers is completely untrue.\"</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Elon Musk  (@elonmusk) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1288722245280464896?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 30, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script>\n\tIn September, Musk tweeted that Gates had \"no clue\" about electric trucks.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7372a80ab50d00184ad0dc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bill Gates\" height=\"2371\" width=\"3161\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bill Gates.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gus Ruelas/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In August, <a href=\"https://www.gatesnotes.com/Energy/Moving-around-in-a-zero-carbon-world\">Gates wrote a blog post</a> about electric vehicles that questioned whether it was practical to make vehicles like 18-wheelers fully electric.</p><p>Though he didn't mention Tesla, the company does produce a semi.</p><p>A few weeks later, a Twitter user asked Musk about his opinion of Gates' comments, to which <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1304792315634966529?s=20\">Musk replied</a>, \"He has no clue.\"</p>\n\tMusk called Gates a \"knucklehead\" for criticizing his coronavirus efforts.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f7370180ab50d00184ad0c8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Elon Musk\" height=\"2250\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Elon Musk.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Patrick Pleul/picture alliance via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>During <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/09/28/opinion/sway-kara-swisher-elon-musk.html?referringSource=articleShare\">a podcast interview</a> published in September, The New York Times' Kara Swisher asked Musk about his feelings about the virus, including whether <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-and-kids-wont-get-coronavirus-vaccine-2020-9\">he planned to get vaccinated</a>.</p><p>Musk defended himself against Gates' comments, saying he'd spent time with Harvard University epidemiologists \"doing antibody studies\" and noting Tesla's work with CureVac.</p><p>\"Gates said something about me not knowing what I was doing,\" Musk told Swisher. \"It's like, 'Hey, knucklehead, we actually make the vaccine machines for CureVac, that company you're invested in.'\"</p>\n\tIn November, Musk surpassed Gates as the world's second-richest person.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fbd15a632f2170011f70d7b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"elon musk happy.JPG\" height=\"1595\" width=\"2126\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Elon Musk celebrates after the launch of a SpaceX Falcon 9 rocket and Crew Dragon spacecraft in May 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Steve Nesius</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Since then, he and Jeff Bezos have flip-flopped as the world's richest. His net worth currently stands at $175 billion, according to <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/billionaires/profiles/elon-r-musk/?sref=BWbpWjRm\">Bloomberg's Billionaires Index</a>.&#160;</p>\n\tGates recently made a jab at Musk's focus on rockets, but did also issue him a rare compliment.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/603d21b687d37600190d06c3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bill Gates\" height=\"1731\" width=\"2308\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bill Gates.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Dursun Aydemir/Anadolu Agency/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>During an appearance <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bill-gates-elon-musk-mars-climate-electric-vehicles-2021-2\">on Kara Swisher's \"Sway\" podcast</a>&#160;in February, Gates said he's not interested in pouring his money into outer space projects like his fellow billionaires, Jeff Bezos and Elon Musk.&#160;</p><p>\"No, I'm not a Mars person. I know a lot of Mars people,\" Gates said. \"I don't think rockets are the solution. But maybe I'm missing something there.\"</p><p>He went on to say that he'd rather spend his money on vaccines here on Earth than on space travel.&#160;</p><p>But Gates did issue a rare compliment to Musk, calling what Musk has accomplished with Tesla \"one of the greatest contributions to climate change anyone's ever made.\"</p><p>\"Underestimating Elon is not a good idea,\" he said.</p>\n\tGates has also taken issue with the mania surrounding cryptocurrencies, which Musk has helped fuel online.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/603d234713b221001876ae65?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bill Gates speaking on a panel .JPG\" height=\"3369\" width=\"4492\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bill Gates.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jason Lee/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>In an interview with Bloomberg, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bill-gates-not-bullish-bitcoin-uses-energy-elon-musk-boom-2021-2-1030111996\">Gates shared his thoughts on cryptocurrencies.</a></p><p>He noted how much energy bitcoin uses, making it not very environmentally friendly. He also warned investors not to dump money into bitcoin like Tesla has.</p><p>\"Elon has tons of money and he's very sophisticated, so I don't worry that his Bitcoin will sort of randomly go up or down,\" Gates told&#160;Bloomberg.</p><p>\"I do think people get bought into these manias, who may not have as much money to spare, so I'm not bullish on Bitcoin, and my general thought would be that, if you have less money than Elon, you should probably watch out,\" he said.&#160;</p>\n\tMusk recently tweeted, then deleted, an anti-vaccine political cartoon about Gates.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60744b412cc1ef0018da12fe?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Elon Musk\" height=\"1499\" width=\"1999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">John Raoux/AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The cartoon, originally created by conservative artist Ben Garrison, depicted Gates as the mastermind of a coronavirus response plan that included making people afraid, locking the country down, and then launching a&#160;\"Mandatory Vaccine Rollout.\"</p><p>In <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-bill-gates-anti-vaxx-cartoon-microsoft-zune-plan-2021-4\">Musk's version</a>, which wasn't sanctioned by Garrison, the last stage of the plan is a \"Zune relaunch,\" in reference to Microsoft's discontinued MP3 player.&#160;</p><p>Musk captioned the image: \"Soon u will feel strange desire for Zune ...\" He deleted the tweet roughly two hours later.&#160;</p><p>Gates has been at the center of conspiracy theories about the coronavirus since last year, including <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bill-gates-spurns-conspiracy-wants-vaccine-to-give-people-microchips-2020-7\">one theory</a> that claimed, without evidence, that Gates wanted to use COVID-19 vaccines to implant microchips into people.&#160;</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
